рд╣рд░рд┐рдГ-рдУрейрдореНред

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╢реНрд░реАрдзрд░рд╛рджрд┐

рд╣рд░рд┐рдГ-рдУрейрдореНред

Eggeling

The ceremonies begin with the preparation of the sacrificial fires. [First, the fivefold lustration successively of the ─Аhavan─лya and Dakshiс╣З─Бgni fire-places, to render them fit for receiving the fire from the G─Бrhapatya or householder’s fire, viz. by thrice sweeping the hearths; thrice besmearing them with gomaya; drawing three lines across them from west to east, or south to north, with the wooden sword (sphya); removing the dust from the lines with the thumb and ring-finger; and thrice sprinkling the lines with water 1.] Then the Adhvaryu performs the agny-uddharaс╣Зa, or twice taking out of the fire from the G─Бrhapatya, and putting it successively on the forepart of the ─Аhavan─лya and Dakshiс╣З─Бgni hearths. After this takes place the agny-anv─Бdh─Бna, or putting (fuel) on the fires, by either the householder or the Adhvaryu; two logs being put on each of the three fires. This may be done in three different ways, viz. first on the ─Аhavan─лya, then on the G─Бrhapatya, and last on the Dakshiс╣З─Бgni, in which case the first log is put on by him whilst muttering the verse Rig-veda X, 128, 1 (Taitt. S. IV, 7, 14, 1), ‘Let there be lustre, O Agni, at my invocations!’ &c., the second log silently. Or the first logs are put on with one of the three mystical words ‘bh┼лr, bhuvaс╕е, svar’ on the G─Бrhapatya, Dakshiс╣З─Бgni, and ─Аhavan─лya successively, and the second logs again silently. Or both logs may be put on silently, the order of fires being in that case the one in which they originate, viz. G─Бrhapatya, ─Аhavan─лya, and Dakshiс╣З─Бgni.

In the afternoon the householder and his wife partake of the vratopan─лya or fast-day food (prepared chiefly of rice, barley, or mudga beans) with clarified butter; whereupon they take the vow in the manner prescribed in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa. In the evening, immediately after sunset, and on the following morning just before sunrise, the householder has, as usual, to perform the Agnihotra, a burnt-offering of fresh milk, which has to be made by him twice daily, with certain exceptions, from the Agny─Бdh─Бna to the end of his life.

Eggeling
  1. He who is about to enter on the vow, touches water 11 whilst standing between the ─Аhavan─лya

and G─Бrhapatya fires, with his face turned towards east. The reason why he touches water is, that man is (sacrificially) impure on account of his speaking untruth; and because by that act an internal purification (is effected),–for water is indeed (sacrificially) pure. ‘After becoming sacrificially pure, I will enter on the vow,’ thus (he thinks); for water is indeed purifying. ‘Having become purified through the purifying one, I will enter on the vow,’ thus (he thinks, and) this is the reason why he touches water.

режреи

рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдордЧреНрдирд┐рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╕рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдХрдВ рд╡реНрд░рддреЛрдкрд╛рдпрдирдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреНрддреЗ- рд╕реЛ рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕рдГ’ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ ‘рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН’ рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрдореН ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрддреБ- рд╣реЗ рд╡реНрд░рддрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ ! рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рдЕрдиреГрддрд╡рджрдирддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ ‘рд╡реНрд░рддрдВ’ рдЪрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред рддрддреНрдХрд░реНрддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрддреЛ рднреВрдпрд╛рд╕рдореН ред рд╢рдХреНрдиреЛрддреЗрд░реНрд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдпрдореН ред рдорджреАрдпрдВ ‘рддрджреН’ рд╡реНрд░рддрдВ рд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрдВ рднрд╡рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ ред

рд╡реНрд░рддрдкрддрд┐рдкрджрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐- рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реИ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдЙрднрдпрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдпрддреНрд╡рдорддреНрд░- рд╢рдХреЗрдпрдВ рд░рд╛рдзреНрдпрддрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЪ рд╣реЗрддреБрдорд╛рд╣- рдирд╛рддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рддрд┐рд░реЛрд╣рд┐рддрдореН’ рдЕрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдкрджрдореН 12 рее реи рее

Eggeling
  1. Looking towards the (─Аhavan─лya) fire 13, he enters on the vow, with the text (V─Бj. S. I, 5 a): ‘O Agni, Lord of Vows! I will keep the vow! may I be equal to it, may I succeed in it!’ For Agni is Lord of Vows to the gods, and it is to him therefore that he addresses these words. In the words, ‘I will observe the vow; may I be equal to it; may I succeed in it,’ there is nothing that requires explanation.

Eggeling
  1. After the completion (of the sacrifice) he divests himself (of the vow), with the text (V─Бj. S. II, 28 a), ‘O Agni, Lord of Vows! I have kept the vow; I have been equal to it; I have succeeded in

it;’ for he who has attained the completion of the sacrifice, has indeed been equal to it; and he who has attained the completion of the sacrifice, has succeeded in it. It is in this way that most (sacrificers) will probably enter on the vow; but one may also enter on it in the following way.

  1. Twofold, verily, is this, there is no third, viz. truth and untruth. And verily the gods are the truth, and man is the untruth. Therefore in saying (V─Бj. S. I, 5 b), ‘I now enter from untruth into truth,’ he passes from the men to the gods 17.

  1. Let him then only speak what is true; for this vow indeed the gods do keep, that they speak the truth; and for this reason they are glorious: glorious therefore is he who, knowing this, speaks the truth.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

“рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡реНрд░рддрдкрддреЗтАЭ рдЗрддрд┐ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╡рддреН рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗрдгрд╛рднреНрдпреБрдкреЗрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡реНрд░рддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╕рд░реНрдЬрдирдорд╛рд╣- рдЕрде рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдерд┐рдд рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╕рд░реНрдЬрдирдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдорд░реНрдердГ 20ред рд╡реНрд░рддреЛрдкрд╛рдпрдирд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧрд╣рдВ рдп рдПрд╡ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐, рд╡реНрд░рддрдВ рдореБрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕ рдПрд╡ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ ‘рдЗрджрдорд╕реНрдорд┐’; рди рддреБ рд╡реНрд░рддрд╕рдордп рдЗрд╡ рджреЗрд╡рдГ ред рдЗрджрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдирдкреБрдВрд╕рдХрдореН ред рдирдиреНрд╡рд╕реМ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рд╡реНрд░рддрд╕рдордпреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдПрд╡, рддрддреНрдХрд┐рдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рдп рдПрд╡ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐ рд╕ рдПрд╡реЗрджрдорд╕реНрдореАрддрд┐ ? Eggeling
  1. After the completion (of the sacrifice) he divests himself (of the vow), with the text (V─Бj. S. II, 28 b): ‘Now I am he who I really am.’ For, in entering upon the vow, he becomes, as it were, nonhuman; and as it would not be becoming for him to say, ‘I enter from truth into untruth;’ and as, in fact, he now again becomes man, let him therefore divest himself (of the vow), with the text: ‘Now I am he who I really am.’

Eggeling
  1. Now then of the eating (or) fasting 21. And on this point ─Аsh─Бс╕Нс╕еa S─Бvayasa, on the one hand, was of opinion that the vow consisted in fasting. For assuredly, (he argued,) the gods see through the mind of man; they know that, when he enters on this

vow, he means to sacrifice to them the next morning. Therefore all the gods betake themselves to his house, and abide by (him or the fires, upa-vas) in his house; whence this (day) is called upa-vasatha 22.

Eggeling
  1. Now, as it would even be unbecoming for him to take food, before men (who are staying with him as his guests) have eaten; how much more would it be so, if he were to take food before the gods (who are staying with him) have eaten: let him therefore take no food at all.

Eggeling
  1. Y─Бj├▒avalkya, on the other hand, said: ‘If he does not eat, he thereby becomes a sacrificer to the Manes; and if he does eat, he eats before the gods have eaten: let him therefore eat what, when eaten, counts as not eaten.’ For that of which no offering is made, even though it is eaten, is considered as not eaten. When he therefore eats, he does not become a sacrificer to the Manes; and by eating of that of which no offering is made, he does not eat before the gods have eaten.

рдЕрде рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд╛рджреГрдХреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдпрджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН ? рдЗрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛рд╣- рд╕ рд╡рд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЖрд░рдгреНрдпрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрджрд░реНрд╢рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡реНрдпрддрд┐рд░рд┐рдХреНрддреЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН ред тАШрд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдВтАШ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЛрджреНрднрд╡рдВ рдлрд▓рдореН ред рднреБрдХреНрддреЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрддреНрд╡реЗ рдореБрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рдгрдпрддрд┐- рддрджреБ рд╣реЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдирд╛рдо рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН, рддрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛ ‘рд╡рд╛рд░реНрд╖реНрдгрдГтАШ рддрд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рдо тАШрд╡рд░реНрдХреБрдГтАЩ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдореБрдиреЗрд░реНрдорддрдордкрд╡рджрддрд┐- рддрджреБ рддрдереЗрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╣реЗрддреБрдГ- рд╡реНрд░реАрд╣рд┐рдпрд╡рдпреЛрд░рд┐рддрд┐ ред тАШрд╢рдореАрдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрдВтАШ рддрд┐рд▓рдорд╛рд╖рд╛рджрд┐ ред рдЙрдкрдЪрд┐рдиреЛрддреАрддрд┐ тАШрдЙрдкрдЪрдореНтАШ ред рдЕрд▓реНрдкреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдорд╛рд╖рдкрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЗрди рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рд╡реНрд░реАрд╣рд┐рдкрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рдЪрддреБрд░рд╛рдиреН рдпрд╛рдорд╛рдирдкрд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрдореН тАШрдЙрдкрдЪрд┐рддрдВтАШ рдмрд╣реБ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рддрджрд╛рд╣- рд╡реНрд░реАрд╣рд┐рдпрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ ред рдЕрддреЛ рдорд╛рд╖реЛрдкрдпреЛрдЧреЗ рд╡реНрд░реАрд╣рд┐рдпрд╡рд╛рд╡реЗрд╡ рдпрдд рдЙрдкрдпреБрдХреНрддреМ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдореН, рдЕрддрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ рди рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЕрддреЛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрдорд╛рд░рдгреНрдпрдореЗрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрдиреАрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ 25 ред рддрджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рд╕рдХреГрджрд╢рдирдореН рее резреж рее

Eggeling
  1. Let him therefore eat only what grows in the forest, be it forest plants or the fruit of trees. And in regard to this point Barku V─Бrshс╣Зa said: ‘Cook ye beans for me, for no offering is made of them!’ This, however, he should not do; for pulse

serves as an addition to rice and barley; and hence he increases the rice and barley by means of it: let him therefore eat only what grows in the forest.

Eggeling
  1. Let him sleep that night in the house of the ─Аhavan─лya fire or in the house of the G─Бrhapatya fire. For he who enters on the vow approaches the gods; and he sleeps in the midst of those very gods whom he approaches. Let him sleep on the ground 27; for from below, as it were, one serves one’s superior.

After the morning’s performance of the Agnihotra and the subsequent rising of the sun, the sacrificer chooses his Brahman, or superintending priest. [In the first place he gets six seats ready, covered with sacrificial grass: two of these, to be used by the Brahman and sacrificer during the ceremony of election, are placed somewhere on the north side of the sacrificial ground; another south of the ─Аhavan─лya fire, to serve for the Brahman’s permanent seat (brahmas─Бdanam), and west of the latter (placed so as to be quite close to the altar to be constructed hereafter, cf. K─Бty. ┼Ъr. I, 8, 28), the sacrificer’s permanent seat; finally a seat north of each of the two fires, the G─Бrhapatya and the ─Аhavan─лya, to be used by the Adhvaryu on certain occasions. The sacrificer and future Brahman then having seated themselves on the two first-mentioned seats on the north side, the former with his face turned northward, and the latter looking toward east; the sacrificer, holding the wooden sword (sphya) in his left hand, touches the right knee of the Brahman with his right hand, in which he holds barley-corns and] chooses him for his Brahman with the formula: [‘Thou, of such and such a family, N.N. ┼Ъarman! we are about to perform the Full-moon sacrifice,’] ‘O Lord of the earth! Lord of the world! Lord of the great universe! we choose thee for our Brahman!’ The chosen one then mutters (cf. V─Бj. S. p. 57): ‘I am the lord of the earth, I lord of the world, I lord of the great universe (mah─Бbh┼лta)! earth! ether! heaven! O God Savitr╠е, thee they choose for their Brahman, their lord of prayer (Br╠еhaspati)!’ &c., ‘Br╠еhaspati is Brahman to the gods, I to the men!’ He (or, according

Eggeling
  1. By way of his first act on the following morning he (the Adhvaryu priest) betakes himself to the water, and brings water forward 30: for

water is (one of the means of) sacrifice. Hence by this his first act he approaches (engages in) the sacrifice; and by bringing (water) forward, he spreads out (prepares) the sacrifice.

Eggeling
  1. He brings it forward with those mysterious words (V─Бj. S. I, 6): ‘Who (or Praj─Бpati) joins (or yokes) thee (to this fire) 33? He joins thee. For what (or, for Praj─Бpati) does he join thee? For that (or him) he joins thee!’ For Praj─Бpati is undefined 34 (mysterious); Praj─Бpati is the sacrifice: hence he thereby yokes (gets ready for the performance) Praj─Бpati, this sacrifice.

Eggeling
  1. The reason why he brings forward water is, that all this (universe) is pervaded by water 35; hence by this his first act he pervades (or gains) all this (universe).

Eggeling
  1. And whatever here in this (sacrifice) the Hotr╠е, or the Adhvaryu, or the Brahman, or the ─Аgn─лdhra, or the sacrificer himself, does not succeed in accomplishing, all that is thereby obtained (or made good).

Eggeling
  1. Another reason why he brings forward water is this: whilst the gods were engaged in performing sacrifice, the Asuras and Rakshas forbade (raksh)

them, saying, ‘Ye shall not sacrifice!’ and because they forbade (raksh), they are called Rakshas.

Eggeling
  1. The gods then perceived this thunderbolt, to wit, the water: the water is a thunderbolt, for the water is indeed a thunderbolt; hence wherever it goes, it produces a hollow (or depression of ground); and whatever it comes near, it destroys (lit. it burns up). Thereupon they took up that thunderbolt, and in its safe and foeless shelter they spread (performed) the sacrifice. And thus he (the Adhvaryu priest) likewise takes up this thunderbolt, and in its safe and foeless shelter spreads the sacrifice. This is the reason why he brings forward water.

Eggeling
  1. After pouring out some of it (into the jug) he puts it down north of the G─Бrhapatya fire. For water (ap) is female and fire (agni) is male; and the G─Бrhapatya is a house: hence a copulation productive of offspring is thereby effected in this house. Now he who brings forward the water, takes up a thunderbolt; but when he takes up the thunderbolt, he cannot do so unless he is firmly placed; for otherwise it destroys him.

Eggeling
  1. The reason then why he places it near the G─Бrhapatya fire is, that the G─Бrhapatya is a house, and a house is a safe resting-place; so that he thereby stands firmly in a house, and therefore in a safe resting-place: in this way that thunderbolt does not destroy him,–for this reason he places it near the G─Бrhapatya fire.

Eggeling
  1. He then carries it north of the ─Аhavan─лya fire 42. For water is female and fire is male: hence

a copulation productive of offspring is thereby effected. And in this way alone a regular copulation can take place, since the woman lies on the left (or north) side of the man.

рдПрд╡, рди рдкреБрд░рддреЛ рди рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН ред рдЕрдд рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рдХрд╛рддреНрдпрд╛рдпрдиреЗрди- тАЭрдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗрдгрд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрдБ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдирд┐рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐тАЭ (рд╢реНрд░реМ.рд╕реВ. реи. рей. рей) рдЗрддрд┐ рее реирез рее

Eggeling
  1. Let nobody pass between the water (and the fire), lest by passing between them he should disturb the copulation which is taking place. Let him set the water down without carrying it beyond (the north side of the fire, i.e. not on the eastern side); nor should he put it down before reaching (the north side, i.e. not on the western side). For, if he were to put the water down after carrying it beyond,–there being, as it were, a great rivalry between fire and water,–he would cause this rivalry to break forth on the part of the fire; and when they (the priests and the sacrificer) touch the water of this (vessel), he would, by carrying it and setting it down beyond (the northern side), cause the enemy to rise (spirt) in the fire. If, on the other hand, he were to put it down before gaining (the northern side), he would not gain by it the fulfilment of the wish for which it has been brought forward. Let him therefore put it down exactly north of the ─Аhavan─лya fire.

‘рд╕рдВрд░рднреЗрдд’ ‘рд░рдн рд░рд╛рднрд╕реНрдпреЗ’ (рднреНрд╡рд╛. рдЖ. репрепреп.) рд░рд╛рднрд╕реНрдпрдВ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреЛрдкрдХреНрд░рдордГ, рдХрд┐рдордкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдВ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдирд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдирд╢рддрдкрдерднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН ред

Eggeling
  1. He now strews sacrificial grass all round (the fires) 51, and fetches the utensils, taking two at a

time, viz. the winnowing basket and the Agnihotra ladle, the wooden sword and the potsherds, the wedge and the black antelope skin, the mortar and the pestle, the large and the small mill-stones. These are ten in number; for of ten syllables consists the Vir─Бj (metre), and radiant (vir─Бj) 52 also is the sacrifice: so that he thereby makes the sacrifice resemble the Vir─Бj. The reason why he takes two at a time is, because a pair means strength; for when two undertake anything, there is strength in it. Moreover, a pair represents a productive copulation, so that a productive copulation (of those respective objects) is thereby effected.

  22. 5:1 The primary meaning of upa-vas probably is ’to dwell or abide near (? the gods or fires);’ its secondary and technical meaning being ’to fast,’ whence upavasatha, ‘a fasting or fast-day,’ literally ’the abiding near (? or honouring, the gods or fires).’ Cf. III, 9, 2, 7. The term is more usually applied to the preliminary fast-day of the Soma-sacrifice; but the latter being considered the most solemn and efficacious of sacrificial rites, a strong tendency prevails to establish some kind of connection between it and the other ceremonies.   30. 7:1 He, in the first place, pours water into a jug [usually made of varaс╣Зa wood (Crat├жva Roxburghii), four-cornered, about a span or twelve fingers’ breadths deep and four fingers’ breadths square, and furnished with a handle], puts it down north of the G─Бrhapatya fire, and touches it with the formula: ‘I, the existent, will operate with thee (?tv─Б karishy─Бmi), O existent one!’ He then addresses himself to the Brahman: ‘O Brahman! shall I bring the water forward?’ and to the patron or sacrificer: ‘Sacrificer, restrain thy speech!’ The Brahman,—after muttering the mantra (as he does, with certain modifications, on similar occasions when his permission is asked in the course of the performance): ‘Lead on the sacrifice! gladden the deities! May the sacrificer be on the vault of heaven! Where the world of the seven pious R╠еshis is, thither do thou lead this sacrifice and sacrificer!’–replies aloud: ‘Hail (├╡m)! bring forward!’ ↩︎

  31. тАЭрдЕрдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрдкрд╛рдВрд╢реБтАЭ рдЗрддрд┐, тАЭрдЕрдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╣рд┐ рдордиреЛ рд╜рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╣реНрдпреЗрддрджреНрдпрддреНрддреВрд╖реНрдгреАрдореНтАЭ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЗрд╣реИрд╡ (резред рей ред рел ред резреж=реи ред рек ред рек ред рел) ред ↩︎ ↩︎

  33. 8:1 ‘Ka (i.e. who? or Praj─Бpati) joins thee (i.e. places thee, O water, by the side of the ─Аhavan─лya fire)? (I) . . Casmai (i.e. for what purpose? or, for whom? or, for Praj─Бpati) does he join thee? (!)’ Mah─лdh. Dark is the meaning of these words because of the ambiguity of ka, the interrogative pronoun, which speculative theology also takes for a mystic name of Praj─Бpati. Cf. XI, 5, 4, seq.; Max M├╝ller, History of Ancient Sanskrit Literature, p. 433. ↩︎

  34. 8:2 Cf. also I, 6, 1, 20, where S─Бyaс╣Зa says that Praj─Бpati is anirukta, because he represents all deities. ↩︎

  35. 8:3 A play on the word ─Бpaс╕е (ap), ‘water,’ and the root ─Бp, ’to obtain, to pervade.’ ↩︎

  51. 10:1 K─Бty. ┼Ъr. II, 3, 6: ‘Having strewn sacrificial grass around the fires, beginning on the east side,’ which the Comm. interprets: ‘He strews eastward and northward-pointed grass around first the ─Аhavan─лya, then the G─Бrhapatya, and last the Dakshiс╣З─Бgni, beginning each time on the eastern side, and then moving around from left to right, and turning his right side towards the fire, so as to end on the north side’ (cf. K─Бty. IV, 13, 15). The Paddhati, on the other hand, following ─Аpastamba, interprets it to the effect that on the eastern and western sides he strews the grass with its tops turned northward, and on the southern and northern sides with the tops turned eastward. ↩︎

  52. 11:1 Or, ‘and the sacrifice also is Vir─Бj,’ as the scholiast interprets the passage on the ground that at the performance of the Jyotishс╣нoma 190 stotriy─Б verses are used, and that this number is dividable by ten, the number of syllables in the Vir─Бj metre; cf. Weber, Ind. Streifen I, 36, note 4. See also X, 4, 3, 21, where the fire is identified with the vir─Бj on the ground that there are ten fires, viz. eight dhishс╣Зya fires and the ─Аhavan─лya and G─Бrhapatya. In VIII, 4, 5, 5 vir─Бj is explained as ’that which rules.’ ↩︎
